Sahih Muslim 2882 a
Harith b Abi Rabi'a and 'Abdullah b. Safwan both went to Umm Salama, the Mother of the Faithful, and they asked her about the army which would be sunk in the earth, and this relates to the time when Ibn Zubair (was the governor of Mecca). She reported that Allah's Messenger (ï·º) had said that a seeker of refuge would seek refuge in the Sacred House and an army would be sent to him (in order to kill him) and when it would enter a plain ground, it would be made to sink. I said:

Allah's Messenger, what about him who would be made to accompany this army willy nilly? Thereupon he said: He would be made to sink along with them but he would be raised on the Day of Resurrection on the basis of his intention. Abu Ja'far said. ' This plain, ground means the plain ground of Medina.

05/03/2025, 11:04â€¯pm - Syed Abdullah: Asslamualikum, is this hadith authentic?

Sunan Ibn Majah 3719
It was narrated that Umm Salamah said:
"Abu Bakr went out to trade in Busra, one year before the Prophet (ï·º) died, and with him were Nu`aiman and Suwaibit the sons of Harmalah, who had been present at Badr. Nu`aiman was in charge of the provisions, and Suwaibit was a man who joked a lot. He said to Nu`aiman: 'Feed me'. He said: 'Not until Abu Bakr comes'. He said: 'Then I will have to annoy you'. Then they passed by some people, and Suwaibit said to them: 'Will you buy a slave from me?' They said: 'Yes'. He said 'He is a slave who talks a lot and he will tell you, "I am a free man". If you are going to let him go when he says that to you, do not bother buying him.' They said: 'We will buy him from you.' So they bought him from him in return for ten young she-camels, then they brought him and tied a turban or a rope around his neck. Nu`aiman said: 'This man is making fun of you. I am a free man, not a slave.' They said: 'He has already told us about you; and they took him off.' Then Abu Bakr came and he (Suwaibit) told him about that. So he followed those people and returned their camels to them, and took Nu`aiman back. When they came to the Prophet (ï·º) they told him what had happened, and the Prophet (ï·º) and his companions laughed about it for a year."

(116)Chapter: What Has Been Related About Not Reciting Behind The Imam When The Imam Is Reciting Aloud


Jami` at-Tirmidhi 312
Abu Hurairah narrated:

09/03/2025, 4:37â€¯pm - +91 97913 71056: Is the following Hadeeth and the explanation given with it authentic?
09/03/2025, 4:37â€¯pm - +91 97913 71056: Bad breath during Fasting:

Some people mistakenly think that the bad breath of the fasting person is a good thing, citing the Hadith: 

ÙˆÙÙ„ÙØ®ÙÙ„ÙÙˆÙÙ ÙÙÙ…Ù Ø§Ù„ØµÙ‘ÙØ§Ø¦ÙÙ…Ù Ø£ÙØ·Ù’ÙŠÙØ¨Ù Ø¹ÙÙ†Ù’Ø¯Ù Ø§Ù„Ù„Ù‘ÙÙ‡Ù Ù…ÙÙ†Ù’ Ø±ÙÙŠØ­Ù Ø§Ù„Ù’Ù…ÙØ³Ù’ÙƒÙ
"The smell of the mouth of a fasting person is better in the sight of God than the smell of musk (perfume)." 
["Sahih Bukhari", 5927].
https://sunnah.com/bukhari:5927

This is a wrong understanding of the Hadith.

It is talking about the odour that is generated by the empty stomach, it is not encouraging a lack of hygiene by not brushing your teeth. 

This misunderstanding arose at the time of Mu'adh Ibn Jabbal, and he corrected it:

The Prophet used to brush his teeth, when he was fasting. It is encouraged to brush the teeth during fasting even if its with toothpaste, as long as its not swallowed - according to many scholars.

This is especially important when you meet other people, attend gatherings and meetings, etc.

12/03/2025, 1:40â€¯pm - +91 98744 95221: Males only
1) Try to send the narration in Arabic and text form so it's easier for me

2) Try to mention how you want the answer to be beforehand (summarised, takhrÄ«j, scan, voice message etc) to avoid back and forth and wastage of time

3) You are allowed only one question a day as checking authenticity takes time

4) Avoid discussions that are not related to authenticity. Take them to private

5) Try to consolidate your question in one single message, be clear and unambiguous 

6) Only admins are allowed to answer

7) Wait for the answer as tagging/reminders will not give a faster reply

Note: There can be a difference of opinion on grading but I won't necessarily mention it.
Corrections are welcome privately

1) Try to send the quote (Arabic preferably) in text form

Allah says (in meaning):
*From mankind are those who say: "Our Rabb! Give us (Your Bounties) in this world!" While he has no portion in the Hereafter. And of them are those who say: "Our Rabb! Give us in this world good and in the Hereafter good, and save us from the torment of the Fire." For them there will be alloted a share for what they have earned (good or bad). And Allah is Swift in reward.* [2:200-202]

01/04/2025, 5:41â€¯pm - +971 55 405 3501: translation of the whole point:
The Forty-Fourth Point: That Allah's pleasure with His servant is greater than Paradise and all that is in it. This is because pleasure (Ø±Ø¶Ø§) is an attribute of Allah, whereas Paradise is His creation. Allah, the Exalted, said:

"And the pleasure of Allah is greater." [At-Tawbah: 72]

This statement follows His words:

"Allah has promised the believing men and believing women Gardens beneath which rivers flow, wherein they will abide eternally, and pleasant dwellings in Gardens of perpetual residence. But the pleasure of Allah is greater. That is the supreme success." [At-Tawbah: 72]

This divine pleasure is a reward for their contentment with Him in this world. And since this reward is the greatest of all rewards, its cause must be the best of all deeds.

03/04/2025, 11:21â€¯pm - +91 80868 21261: Ziyadat al-Thiqah (Ø²ÙŠØ§Ø¯Ø© Ø§Ù„Ø«Ù‚Ø©) is an Arabic term meaning "the addition by a trustworthy narrator." In the science of Hadith (Islamic tradition studies), it refers to extra words or details in a narration that are reported by a reliable (thiqah) narrator but not found in other versions of the same Hadith.

Ruling on Ziyadat al-Thiqah:

1. Accepted (Maqbool) if it does not contradict stronger narrations â€“ If a trustworthy narrator adds extra information that aligns with established narrations, scholars generally accept it.


2. Rejected (Mardood) if it contradicts stronger narrations â€“ If the addition conflicts with more authentic or widely accepted reports, it is usually rejected.


3. Analyzed based on context â€“ Scholars compare the chain of narrators (isnad) and content (matn) to determine whether to accept or reject the addition.


Correct?

Hence one must sit in the same place remembering Allah(reciting Quran,doing adkhar,doing dhikr,making Dua etc) till 15-20 mins after sunrise ( for today it would be 6:32 ) and pray 4 rakat duha. 10/04/2025, 10:08â€¯pm - Muzammil New: *Here we distinguish between proven and unproven quotes/narrations*
*[Males only]*

1) Try to send the quote (Arabic preferably) in text form

2) Try to mention how you want the answer to be beforehand (summarised, takhrÄ«j, scan, voice message etc) to avoid back and forth and wastage of time

3) You are allowed only one question within 24H as checking authenticity takes time

4) Avoid messages that are not related to authenticity. Take them to private 

5) Try to consolidate your question in one single message, be clear and unambiguous 

6) Try to search (and mention) the reference beforehand (if possible) to reduce workload on the answerer. Please do not ask about quotes generated by AI

7) Wait for the answer instead of tagging/reminders as they will not give a quicker reply

*Note:* There can be a difference of opinion on the grading but I won't necessarily mention it.
Corrections are welcome privately
